This usage does not constitute an official\nendorsement, either expressed or implied, by the National\nAeronautics and Space Administration.\n\nAvailable from\nNASA Center for Aerospace Information\n7121 Standard Drive\nHanover, MD 21076\n\nAvailable electronically at http://gltrs.grc.nasa.gov\n\nPreface\nThis 12-part report documents the data obtained from various sensor measurements taken\naboard the Russian Express-A2 and Express-A3 spacecraft in Geosynchronous Earth Orbit\n(GEO). These GEO communications satellites, which were designed and built by NPO\nPrikladnoy Mekhaniki (NPO PM) of Zheleznogorsk, Russia, utilize Hall thruster propulsion\nsystems for north-south and east-west station-keeping and as of June 2002, were still\noperating at 80\xc2\xb0 E. and 11\xc2\xb0 W., respectively. Express-A2 was launched on March 12, 2000,\nwhile Express-A3 was launched on June 24, 2000. The diagnostic equipment from which\nthese data were taken includes electric field strength sensors, ion current and energy sensors,\nand pressure sensors. The diagnostics and the Hall thruster propulsion systems are described\nin detail along with lists of tabular data from those diagnostics and propulsion system and\nother satellite systems.\nSpace Power, Inc., now part of Pratt & Whitney\xe2\x80\x99s Chemical Systems Division, under\ncontract NAS3\xe2\x80\x9399151 to the NASA Glenn Research Center, obtained these data over several\nperiods from March 12, 2000, through September 30, 2001. Each of the 12 individual reports\ndescribe, in detail, the propulsion systems as well as the diagnostic sensors utilized.\nFinally, parts 11 and 12 include the requirements to which NPO PM prepared and delivered\nthese data.\nFilename\nCR-2003-212005-PART1.pdf\n\nTitle\nHall Effect Thruster Interactions Data From the Russian\nExpress-A2 and Express-A3 Satellites\nAcquire Express-A2 Xenon Storage Unit number "n"\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\nvii\n\nIntroduction\nThe Express-A #2 Spacecraft has been entered into geostationary orbit on March 12, 2000. The\nspacecraft\xe2\x80\x99s electric jet propulsion based on the SPT-100 stationary plasma thrusters is used to\nprovide both the longitude and inclination orbit control.\nThis Report is issued in accordance with the requirements of the Task #29 under the Contract\n#97-1088-02 and prepared in compliance with agreed upon contents of the sections of the\n\xe2\x80\x9cEXPRESS/T160E Project Express A2 and A3 Data Agreement Document dated on October 29,\n2000\xe2\x80\x9d document.\nThis Document includes the flight operational data for the SPT-100 Propulsion at level of the\nExpress-A #2 Spacecraft for a period of March 12 to June 15, 2000 as well as some SPT-100\nground test data.\nIn this Document all the being measured parameters and their changes are referenced to Moscow\nStandard Time.\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n1\n\n1. Express-A#2 Spacecraft Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem based on\nStationary Plasma Thrusters\n1.1. Mission\nThe Propulsion Subsystem based on the stationary plasma thrusters is designed to produce a\nneed thrust for drifting the spacecraft into a specified point of geostationary orbit and for\nlongitude/latitude orbit station keeping during the spacecraft mission life.\n1.2. Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem Configuration\nThe Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem has a modular design of the functional self-contained\nitems:\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Four Orbit Control Thruster Units (TU1, TU2, TU3, TU4); a general view is\nprovided in Fig. 1;\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Xenon Feed Unit (XFU); a general view of thee Unit is shown in Fig. 2;\n\xe2\x80\xa2 Three Xenon Storage Units (XSU1, XSU2, XSU3); a general view of the Unit is\nshown in Fig. 3.\n\nFig. 1. Orbit Control Thruster Unit\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n2\n\nFig. 2. General View of Xenon Feed Unit\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n3\n\nTemperature\nSensor\n\nFig. 3. General View of Xenon Storage Unit\nThe Units are interconnected by the pipelines.\nControl of the Propulsion Subsystem Functional Items is provided by the Power Processing Unit\n(PPU) linked with the Propulsion Subsystem Items by electric cables.\nExpress-A Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem Functional Diagram is shown in Fig. 4.\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n4\n\nL3\n\nFig. 4. SPT-100 allocation layout\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n8\n\n1.3. Three\nbatteries are installed on the Express-A spacecraft. Layout of batteries allocation with respect to\nthe SPT-100 thrusters is provided in Fig. 8 to Fig. 10. Thrust based on ranging results during East-West and North-South maneuvers\nEffective thrust determination results for Express-A#2 Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem are\ngiven in Table 24.\nTable 24\nAscertain Thruster\nAscertain Thruster No\nEffective Thrust,\nOperating Period\n(N*10-2)\n17/03/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 18/03/2000\nT2C1\n8,03\n19/03/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 20/03/2000\nT2C1\n7,95\n28/04/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 30/04/2000\nRT2C1\n8,15\n08/05/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 09/05/2000\nT1C1\n8,10\n11/05/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 12/05/2000\nRT1C1\n8,25\n15/05/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 28/05/2000\nT3C1, RT3C1\n7,05\n01/06/2000 \xe2\x80\x93 13/06/2000\nT3C1, RT3C1\n7,31\nThrust in the East-West direction for the T1, RT1, T2 and RT2 Thrusters was determined during\ndrifting and transfer phases. Under that the method used to calculate the thrust is finding of such\ncontrol acceleration, which when integrating the differential equations of motion at active flight\nphases permits to obtain the orbit parameters conforming with the ranging data after orbit control\nmaneuver. As initial conditions for the integration were assumed the orbit parameters as\ndetermined on base of the ranging data before orbit control maneuver. Change of orbit\nparameters when performing orbit control maneuver is incommensurably greater than possible\nuncertainty of the orbit parameters based on the ranging data. Therefore, an accuracy of thrust\ndetermination in this case is sufficiently high and the uncertainty does not exceed 2 %.\nFor the North-South orbit control thrusters T3C1 and RT3C1, when determining a mean-integral\nvalue of effective thrust it was assumed that thrust values of all thrusters at all firings to be fell in\na measurement interval are equal. In this case the measurement interval is a time period between\ntwo ranging cycles, of which there are performed SPT-100 thruster firings.\nThe longer the measurement interval, the higher an accuracy of mean-integral thrust value\ncalculation. This is clarified as follows: the longer the measurement interval, the greater the\nchange of orbit parameters due to the SPT-100 thruster firings, and accordingly, the lesser an\ninfluence of possible uncertainties when determining the orbit parameters based on the ranging\ndata.\n1.13. Comments on SPT Operation\nNo any comments on SPT-100 operation within the period of 16/03/00 to 15/06/00 are recorded.\nAll the operations on the Express-A#2 Orbit Control Propulsion Subsystem were performed in\naccordance with the specified logic and no any additional measures were taken.\n\nNASA/CR\xe2\x80\x942003-212005/PART1\n\n32\n\n2. ABSTRACT (Maximum 200 words)\n\nThis 12-part report documents the data obtained from various sensor measurements taken aboard the Russian Express-A2\nand Express-A3 spacecraft in Geosynchronous Earth Orbit (GEO). These GEO communications satellites, which were\ndesigned and built by NPO Prikladnoy Mekhaniki (NPO PM) of Zheleznogorsk, Russia, utilize Hall thruster propulsion\nsystems for north-south and east-west stationkeeping and as of June 2002, were still operating at 80\xc2\xb0 E. and 11\xc2\xb0 W.,\nrespectively. Express-A2 was launched on March 12, 2000, while Express-A3 was launched on June 24, 2000. The\ndiagnostic equipment from which these data were taken includes electric field strength sensors, ion current and energy\nsensors, and pressure sensors. The diagnostics and the Hall thruster propulsion systems are described in detail along with\nlists of tabular data from those diagnostics and propulsion system and other satellite systems. Space Power, Inc., now part\nof Pratt & Whitney\xe2\x80\x99s Chemical Systems Division, under contract NAS3\xe2\x80\x9399151 to the NASA Glenn Research Center,\nobtained these data over several periods from March 12, 2000, through September 30, 2001. Each of the 12 individual\nreports describe, in detail, the propulsion systems as well as the diagnostic sensors utilized. Finally, parts 11 and 12\ninclude the requirements to which NPO PM prepared and delivered these data.\n14. SUBJECT TERMS\n\n15.
